‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§É

‡§®‡§æ‡§ï‡§∏‡§¶ ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§®‡§æ‡§ï‡§∏‡§¶‡•ã ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§™‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡•á‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§ï‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§∏‡§æ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§™‡§ß‡§æ‡§®‡§Æ‡•á‡§§‡§æ‡§∏‡•Å ‡§¶‡§∂‡§∏‡•Å ‡§ï‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§™‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á 1 ‡•§ ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§æ ‡§µ‡•à ‡§®‡§æ‡§ï‡§∏‡§¶‡•ã ‡§®‡§æ‡§ï‡•á ‡§Ö‡§∏‡•Ä‡§¶‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§§‡•á‡§∑‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ö‡§æ‡§ß‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§∂‡§∞‡•Ä‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§ø ‡§á‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§ï‡§æ ‡§Ö‡§™‡§ø ‡§§‡§¶‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ ‡§è‡§µ‡•á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§®‡§æ‡§ï‡§∏‡§¶‡•ã ‡§Ø‡§ú‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•ã ‡§Ω‡§™‡§ø ‡§Ü‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∞‡•Ç‡§™‡§æ ‡§è‡§µ‡§Æ‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç ‡§§‡§Æ‡•Å‡§™‡§¶‡§ß‡•Å‡§É ‡§â‡§™‡§¶‡§ß‡§æ‡§§‡§ø ‡§á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§§‡§§‡•ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§•‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§≠‡•á‡§¶‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç ‡•• ‡•ß ‡••

Eggeling
  1. He lays down the NƒÅkasads (firmament-seated bricks): the firmament-seated ones, assuredly, are the gods. In this (layer) that whole fire-altar becomes completed, and therein these (bricks are) the firmament (nƒÅka), the world of heaven: it is therein that the gods seated themselves; and inasmuch as the gods seated themselves on that firmament, in the world of heaven, the gods are the firmament-seated. And in like manner does the Sacrificer, when he lays down these (bricks), now seat himself on that firmament, in the world of heaven.

‡•¶‡•®

‡§Ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§µ ‡§®‡§æ‡§ï‡§∏‡§¶ ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§è‡§§‡§æ‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§≠‡•á‡§¶‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡§®‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§¶‡§∂‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•Ä‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ö‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡•§ ‡§§‡§æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§∞‡•Å‡§™‡§æ‡§Ø‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§®‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§µ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡•Ä‡§¶‡§ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§Ø‡§ú‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•ã ‡§Ω‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡•á ‡§§‡§æ ‡§è‡§µ‡•ã‡§™‡§æ‡§Ø‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§æ‡§É ‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§ï‡•á ‡§∏‡•Ä‡§¶‡§§‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø ‡§®‡§æ‡§ï‡§∏‡§¶‡§É ‡§® ‡§ï‡§∞‡§£‡§∏‡§æ‡§ß‡§®‡§É ‡§ò‡§û‡•ç ‡•§ ‡§ï‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•Å ‡§ï‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§™‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡§ø‡§§‡§É ‡•• ‡•® ‡•• ‡•© ‡••

Eggeling
  1. And, again, why he lays down the NƒÅkasads. Now at that time the gods saw that firmament, the world of heaven, these StomabhƒÅgƒÅs 2. They spake,

‘Think ye upon this, how we may seat ourselves on that firmament, in the world of heaven!’ They spake,

‘Meditate ye! seek ye a layer!’ whereby, indeed, they said, ‘Seek ye this, how we may seat ourselves on this firmament, in the world of heaven!’

Eggeling
  1. Whilst meditating, they saw these bricks, the NƒÅkasads, and placed them on (the altar): by means of them they seated themselves on that firmament, in the world of heaven; and inasmuch as through them they seated themselves (sad) on that firmament (nƒÅka), in the world of heaven, these are the NƒÅka-sad (bricks); and in like manner does the Sacrificer, when he lays down these (bricks), now seat himself on that firmament, in the world of heaven.

Eggeling
  1. He places them in the (four) quarters; for that firmament, the world of heaven, is the quarters: he thus establishes them in the world of heaven. On the range of the RÃ•tavyƒÅs (he places them); for the RÃ•tavyƒÅs (seasonal bricks) are the year, and the world of heaven is the year: it is in the world of heaven he thus establishes them. Within the StomabhƒÅgƒÅs (he places them); for this is the firmament, the world of heaven: it is therein he thus establishes them.

‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§ú‡§ó‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§ß‡§æ‡§∞‡§Ø‡§§ ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§Æ‡§®‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡§π‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∂‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç ‡•§ (‡§§‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§™‡§ø ‡§® Eggeling
  1. In front he lays down one, with (VƒÅj. S. XV, 10), ‘Queen thou art, the Eastern region,’ for a queen indeed the eastern region is;–‘The divine Vasus are thine overlords 5,’ for the divine Vasus are indeed the overlords of that region;–‘Agni is the repeller of shafts,’ for Agni, indeed, is here the repeller of shafts;–‘The TrivrÃ•t-Stoma may uphold thee on earth!’ for by the threefold hymn(-form) this one is indeed upheld on earth;–‘The ƒÄjya-≈õastra may support thee for steadiness‚Äô sake 6!’ for by the ƒÄjya-≈õastra it is indeed supported on earth for steadiness‚Äô sake;–’the Rathantara-sƒÅman for stability in the air!’ for by the Rathantara-sƒÅman it is indeed established in the air;–‘May the RÃ•shis, the first-born, magnify 7 thee among the gods!’–the RÃ•shis, the first-born, doubtless, are the vital airs 8, for they are the first-born Brahman 9;–‘with the measure, the width of the sky!’–that is, ‘as great as the sky is, so much in width may they broaden thee!’–

‘And he, the upholder, and the overlord,’–these two are speech and mind, for these two uphold everything here;–‘may they all, of one mind, settle thee, and the Sacrificer, on the back of the firmament, in the world of heaven!’ as the text, so its import.

‡•¶‡•¨

(‡§∞·≥ò) ‡§Ö·≥ò‡§• ‡§¶‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§£‡§§‡§É·≥ò‡••

‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§É

[‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§™‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§Æ‡•á]

Eggeling
  1. Then on the right (south) side (he lays down one 12), with (VƒÅj. S. XV, 11), ‘Wide-ruling thou art, the southern region,’ for wide-ruling indeed is that southern region;–‘The divine Rudras are thine overlords,’ for the divine Rudras are indeed the overlords of that region;–‘Indra is the repeller of shafts,’ for Indra, indeed, is here the repeller of shafts;–‘The Pa√±cada≈õa-stoma may uphold thee on earth!’ for by the fifteenfold hymn it is indeed upheld on earth;–‘The Pra√ºga-≈õastra may support thee for steadiness‚Äô sake!’ for by the Pra√ºga-≈õastra it is indeed supported on earth for steadiness‚Äô sake;–’the BrÃ•hat-sƒÅman for stability in the air!’ for by the BrÃ•hat-sƒÅman it is indeed established in the air;–‘May the RÃ•shis, the first-born, magnify thee among gods . . .!’ the import of this (and the rest) has been explained.

(‡§§‡•ç‡§∏) ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ·≥ò‡§°‡§∏‡§ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•Ä·≥ò‡§ö‡•Ä ‡§¶‡§ø‡§ó‡§ø·≥ò‡§§‡§ø ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ·≥ò‡§°‡•ç‡§¢ ‡§®‡§æ·≥ò‡§Æ‡•à‡§∑‡§æ·≥ò ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•Ä·≥ò‡§ö‡§ø ‡§¶‡§ø·≥ò‡§ó‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ·≥ò‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§æ ‡§Ω‡§Ö·≥ò‡§ß‡§ø‡§™‡§§‡§Ø ‡§Ω‡§á·≥ò‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ·≥ò ‡§π‡•à‡§§·≥ò‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡•à ‡§¶‡§ø‡§∂‡•ã·≥ò ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§æ ‡§Ω‡§Ö·≥ò‡§ß‡§ø‡§™‡§§‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§µ‡•ç‡§µ·≥ò‡§∞‡•Å‡§£‡•ã ‡§π‡•á‡§§‡•Ä‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç·≥ò ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•á·≥ò‡§§‡§ø ‡§µ‡•ç‡§µ·≥ò‡§∞‡•Å‡§£‡•ã ‡§π‡•à‡§µ‡§æ·≥ò‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§π‡•á‡§§‡•Ä‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç·≥ò ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§æ·≥ò ‡§∏‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§¶‡§∂·≥ò‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ã·≥ò‡§Æ‡§É ‡§™‡•É‡§•‡§ø‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ·≥ò·≥´‡§Å·≥ò ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø·≥ò‡§§‡§ø ‡§∏‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§¶‡§∂‡•á·≥ò‡§® ‡§π‡•à‡§∑‡§æ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ã·≥ò‡§Æ‡•á‡§® ‡§™‡•É‡§•‡§ø‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ·≥ò·≥´‡§Å·≥ò ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡§æ·≥ò ‡§Æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡•Ä·≥ò‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§•‡§Æ·≥ò‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ‡§Ø‡•à ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§≠‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø·≥ò‡§§‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡•Ä·≥ò‡§Ø‡•á‡§® ‡§π‡•à·≥ò‡§∑‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§•‡•á‡§®‡§æ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ‡§Ø‡•à ‡§™‡•É‡§•‡§ø‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ·≥ò·≥´‡§Å·≥ò ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§¨‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ·≥ò ‡§µ‡•ç‡§µ‡•à‡§∞‡•Ç‡§™·≥´‡§Å·≥≠ ‡§∏‡§æ‡§Æ·≥ò ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞·≥ò‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§Ω‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§§·≥ò‡§∞‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑ ‡§Ω‡§á·≥ò‡§§‡§ø ‡§µ‡•ç‡§µ‡•à‡§∞‡•Ç‡§™‡•á·≥ò‡§£ ‡§π‡•à‡§∑‡§æ ‡§∏‡§æ·≥ò‡§Æ‡•ç‡§®‡§æ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞·≥ò‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§ø‡§§‡§æ ‡§Ω‡§®‡•ç‡§§·≥ò‡§∞‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑ ‡§Ω‡§ã·≥ò‡§∑‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§•‡§Æ‡§ú‡§æ·≥ò ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡•á‡§∑‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø·≥ò‡§§‡§ø ‡§§·≥ò‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ã ‡§¨·≥ò‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡•Å‡§É‡••

Eggeling
  1. Then behind (he lays down one), with (VƒÅj. S. XV, 12), ‘All-ruling thou art, the western region,’ for all-ruling indeed is that western region;–‘The divine ƒÄdityas are thine overlords,’ for the divine ƒÄdityas are indeed the overlords of that region;–‘Varu·πáa is the repeller of shafts,’ for Varu·πáa, indeed, is here the repeller of shafts;–‘The Saptada≈õa-stoma may uphold thee on

earth!’ for by the seventeenfold hymn it is indeed upheld on earth;–‘The Marutvatƒ´ya-≈õastra may support thee for steadiness‚Äô sake!’ for by the Marutvatƒ´ya-≈õastra it is indeed supported on earth for steadiness‚Äô sake;–’the Vair≈´pa-sƒÅman for stability in the air!’ for by the Vair≈´pa-sƒÅman it is indeed established in the air;–‘May the RÃ•shis, the first-born, magnify thee among the gods . . .!’ the import of this has been explained.

‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§É

[‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§™‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§Æ‡•á]

Eggeling
  1. Then on the left (north) side (he lays down one), with (VƒÅj. S. XV, 13), ‘Self-ruling thou art, the northern region,’ for self-ruling that northern region indeed is; ‘The divine Maruts are thine overlords,’ for the divine Maruts are indeed the overlords of that region;–‘Soma is the repeller of shafts,’ for Soma, indeed, is here the repeller of shafts;–‘The Ekavi·πÅ≈õa-stoma may uphold thee on earth!’ for by the twenty-one-fold hymn this one is indeed upheld on earth;–‘The Nishkevalya-≈õastra may support thee for steadiness‚Äô sake!’ for by the Nishkevalya-≈õastra it is indeed supported on earth for steadiness‚Äô sake;–’the VairƒÅja-sƒÅman for stability in the air!’ for by the VairƒÅja-sƒÅman it is indeed established in the air;–‘May the RÃ•shis, the first-born, magnify thee among the gods . . .!’ the import of this has been explained.

‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§É

[‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§™‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§Æ‡•á]

Eggeling
  1. Then in the middle (he lays down one 14), with (VƒÅj. S. XV, 14), ‘The sovereign mistress thou art, the Great region!’ for the sovereign mistress that great region indeed is;–’the All-gods are

thine overlords,’ for the All-gods are indeed the overlords of that region;–‘BrÃ•haspati is the repeller of shafts,’ for BrÃ•haspati, indeed, is here the repeller of shafts;–‘The Tri·πáava- and Trayastri·πÅ≈õa-stomas may uphold thee on earth;’–for by the twenty-nine-fold and thirty-three-fold hymns this one is indeed upheld on earth;–‘The Vai≈õvadeva- and ƒÄgnimƒÅruta-≈õastras may support thee for steadiness‚Äô sake!’ for by the Vai≈õvadeva- and ƒÄgnimƒÅruta-≈õastras it is indeed supported on earth for steadiness‚Äô sake;–‘May the RÃ•shis, the first-born, magnify thee among the gods . . .!’ the import of this has been explained.

Eggeling
  1. Thus much, indeed, is the whole sacrifice, and the sacrifice is the self of the gods: it was after making the sacrifice their own self that the gods seated themselves on that firmament, in the world of heaven; and in like manner does the Sacrificer now, after making the sacrifice his own self, seat himself on that firmament, in the world of heaven.

Eggeling
  1. He then lays down the Pa√±cac≈´·∏çƒÅ (‘five-knobbed’) bricks; for the NƒÅkasads are (parts of) the sacrifice, and so indeed are the Pa√±cac≈´·∏çƒÅs the sacrifice: the NƒÅkasads are these four sacrificial priests together with the Sacrificer as the fifth; and the Pa√±cac≈´·∏çƒÅs are the HotrƒÅs 16. Now the HotrƒÅs are additional (to the officiating staff, or to the HotrÃ•) and whatever is additional is an excrescence (c≈´·∏ça); and hence, as they are five additional (bricks), they are (called) Pa√±cac≈´·∏çƒÅs 17.

Eggeling
  1. And, again, as to why he lays down the NƒÅkasad-Pa√±cac≈´·∏çƒÅs;–it is for the sake of completeness; for the NƒÅkasads are the self, and the Pa√±cac≈´·∏çƒÅs the mate, and this, the mate, doubtless, is one half of the self; for when one is with his mate 18, then he is whole and complete.

Eggeling
  1. And, again, as to why he lays down the NƒÅkasad-Pa√±cac≈´·∏çƒÅs;–the NƒÅkasads are the self, and the Pa√±cac≈´·∏çƒÅs are offspring (or subjects) 19. Now progeny is something additional to the self, and whatever is additional is an excrescence; and hence, as they are five additional ones, they are (called) Pa√±cac≈´·∏çƒÅs.

Eggeling
  1. And, again, as to why he lays down the NƒÅkasad-Pa√±cac≈´·∏çƒÅs;–the NƒÅkasads are the regions, and the Pa√±cac≈´·∏çƒÅs, too, are the regions: what five regions there are on this side of yonder sun, they are the NƒÅkasads, and those which are on the other side are the Pa√±cac≈´·∏çƒÅs. Now those regions which are on the other side of yonder sun are additional, and what is additional is an excrescence (c≈´·∏ça): and hence, as they are five additional ones, they are called Pa√±cac≈´·∏çƒÅs.

Eggeling
  1. And, again, as to why he lays down the Pa√±cac≈´·∏çƒÅs. Now, at that time the gods were afraid lest the fiends, the Rakshas, should destroy

these worlds of theirs from above. They put those protectors over these worlds, to wit, those shafts and missiles; and in like manner does the Sacrificer now put those protectors over these worlds, to wit, those shafts and missiles.

‡§π‡•á‡§§‡§ø‡§É ‡§™‡•å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡•á‡§Ø‡•ã, ‡§µ‡§ß‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•á‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§Ø‡§¶‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§Ω‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ò‡•ç‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø- ‡§∏ ‡§™‡•å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡•á‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§µ‡§ß‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•á‡§§‡§ø‡§É ‡•§ “‡§§‡•á‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§®‡§Æ‡•ã ‡§Ö‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å”- ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§§‡•á‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§è‡§µ ‡§®‡§Æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ “‡§§‡•á ‡§®‡•ã ‡§Æ‡•É‡§°‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•Å”- ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§§ ‡§è‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡•à ‡§Æ‡•É‡§°‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ “‡§§‡•á ‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§Æ‡•ã ‡§Ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§®‡•ã ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§ø ‡§§‡§Æ‡•á‡§∑‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ú‡§Æ‡•ç‡§≠‡•á ‡§¶‡§ß‡•ç‡§Æ‡§É”- (‡§µ‡§æ. ‡§∏‡§Ç. ‡•ß‡•´ ‡•§ ‡•ß‡•´) ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§ø, ‡§Ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡•à‡§®‡§Ç ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§ø- ‡§§‡§Æ‡•á‡§∑‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ú‡§Æ‡•ç‡§≠‡•á ‡§¶‡§ß‡§æ‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§Ö‡§Æ‡•Å‡§Æ‡•á‡§∑‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ú‡§Æ‡•ç‡§≠‡•á ‡§¶‡§ß‡§æ‡§Æ‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø ‡§π ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç- ‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç ‡•§ ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§® ‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§Ö‡§™‡§ø ‡§§‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡•á‡§§ ‡•§ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•ã ‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§µ ‡§∏‡§É- ‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ‡§Ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§ø ‡•• ‡•ß‡•¨ ‡••

‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§É

[‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§™‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§¶‡§∂‡•á]

Eggeling
  1. He places one in front, with (VƒÅj. S. XV, 15), ‘This one in front, the yellow-haired one,’–Agni, no doubt, is in front; and as ’to his saying of him as (being) ‘in front,’ it is because they take him out (of the GƒÅrhapatya hearth) towards the front 22, and attend upon him towards the front; and as to why he calls him yellow-haired, it is because Agni is, as it were, yellow;–’the sun-rayed one,’ for Agni’s rays are like those of the sun;–‘and RathagrÃ•tsa and Rathaujas 23, his commander and his chieftain,’ the two spring-months are these two;–‘and the nymphs Pu√±jikasthalƒÅ and KratusthalƒÅ 24,’–‘quarter and intermediate quarter,’ said MƒÅhitthi; but army and battle these two are;–‘mordacious beasts the shaft, manslaughter the missile,’–inasmuch as they fight in army and battle, those mordacious beasts are the shaft; ‘manslaughter the missile,’–inasmuch as they slay one another, manslaughter is the missile;–’to them be homage!’ it is to them he pays homage;–‘be they gracious unto us!’ they are indeed gracious to him;–‘he whom we hate, and he who hates us,

him we put into their jaws!’ whomsoever he hates, and whoever hates him, him he puts into their jaws. ‘N. N. I put into their jaws,’ thus he may name him whom he hates, and thereafter he will not be there any more. Let him disregard this also, for indeed marked out of himself is he whom he who knows this hates.

‡•ß‡•≠

‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏-‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§§‡§ø‡§É

(‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•ç‡§Ø·≥ò) ‡§Ö·≥ò‡§• ‡§¶‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§£‡§§‡§É·≥ò‡••
(‡§§‡•ã ‡§Ω‡§Ø‡§Ç·≥ò) ‡§Ö‡§Ø‡§Ç·≥ò ‡§¶‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§£‡§æ·≥ò ‡§µ‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ·≥ò‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡•á·≥ò‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•à·≥ò ‡§µ‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ø‡•Å·≥ò‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ·≥ò‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ·≥ò ‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§Ω‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§™·≥ò‡§µ‡§§ ‡§Ω‡§è‡§∑·≥ò ‡§π‡•Ä‡§¶·≥´‡§Å·≥≠ ‡§∏·≥ò‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã·≥ò‡§§‡§ø ‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§æ·≥ò‡§π ‡§¶‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§£‡•á·≥ò‡§§‡§ø ‡§§·≥ò‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡•á‡§∑·≥ò ‡§¶‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø·≥ò‡§£‡•à‡§µ ‡§≠‡•Ç·≥ò‡§Ø‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§§‡§ø ‡§§·≥ò‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∞‡§•‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§®·≥ò‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§∞·≥ò‡§•‡•á‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§∏‡•á‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡•Ä‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ·≥ò‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§µ‡§ø·≥ò‡§§‡§ø ‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡•à·≥ò‡§∑‡•ç‡§Æ‡•å ‡§§‡§æ·≥ò‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•Ç·≥ò ‡§Æ‡•á‡§®‡§ï‡§æ·≥ò ‡§ö ‡§∏‡§π‡§ú‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ·≥ò ‡§ö‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§∏‡§∞·≥ò‡§∏‡§æ‡§µ‡§ø·≥ò‡§§‡§ø ‡§¶‡§ø·≥ò‡§ï‡•ç‡§ö‡•ã‡§™‡§¶‡§ø‡§∂‡§æ ‡§ö‡•á·≥ò‡§§‡§ø ‡§π ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§π ‡§Æ‡§æ·≥ò‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§∞‡§ø‡§Æ‡•á ‡§§‡•Å ‡§§‡•á ‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ·≥ò‡§µ‡§æ‡§™‡•É‡§•‡§ø‡§µ‡•Ä·≥ò ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•Å‡§ß‡§æ·≥ò‡§®‡§æ ‡§π‡•á‡§§‡•Ä ‡§∞·≥ò‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§æ·≥´‡§Å·≥≠‡§∏‡§ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞·≥ò‡§π‡•á‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡§ø·≥ò‡§§‡§ø ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•Å‡§ß‡§æ·≥ò‡§®‡§æ ‡§π‡•à‡§µ‡§æ·≥ò‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§π‡•á‡§§‡•Ä ‡§∞·≥ò‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§æ·≥´‡§Å·≥≠‡§∏‡§ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞·≥ò‡§π‡•á‡§§‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•á·≥ò‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã·≥ò ‡§®·≥ò‡§Æ‡•ã ‡§Ω‡§Ö‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø·≥ò‡§§‡§ø ‡§§·≥ò‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ã ‡§¨·≥ò‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡•Å‡§É‡••

(‡•®) ‡§Ö‡§• ‡§¶‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§£‡§§‡§É ‡•§ “‡§Ö‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§¶‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§£‡§æ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ”- ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§Ö‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•à ‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§Ω‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§™‡§µ‡§§‡•á ‡•§ ‡§è‡§∑ ‡§π‡•Ä‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§§‡§¶‡•ç ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§æ‡§π- ‡§¶‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§£‡•á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡•á‡§∑ ‡§¶‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§£‡•à‡§µ ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§Ø‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§æ‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ “‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∞‡§•‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§®‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§∞‡§•‡•á‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§∏‡•á‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡•Ä‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡•å”- ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡•à‡§∑‡•ç‡§Æ‡•å ‡§§‡§æ‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•Ç ‡•§ “‡§Æ‡•á‡§®‡§ï‡§æ ‡§ö ‡§∏‡§π‡§ú‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§ö‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§∏‡§∞‡§∏‡•å”- ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§¶‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§ö‡•ã‡§™‡§¶‡§ø‡§∂‡§æ ‡§ö‡•á‡§§‡§ø ‡§π ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§π ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§É ‡•§ ‡§á‡§Æ‡•á ‡§§‡•Å ‡§§‡•á ‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§µ‡§æ‡§™‡•É‡§•‡§ø‡§µ‡•Ä ‡•§ “‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•Å‡§ß‡§æ‡§®‡§æ ‡§π‡•á‡§§‡•Ä ‡§∞‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∏‡§ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•á‡§§‡§ø‡§É”- ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•Å‡§ß‡§æ‡§®‡§æ ‡§π‡•à‡§µ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§π‡•á‡§§‡•Ä ‡§∞‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∏‡§ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•á‡§§‡§ø‡§É ‡•§ “‡§§‡•á‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§®‡§Æ‡•ã ‡§Ö‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å”- (‡§µ‡§æ. ‡§∏‡§Ç. ‡•ß‡•´ ‡•§ ‡•ß‡•¨) ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ã ‡§¨‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡•Å‡§É ‡•• ‡•ß‡•≠ ‡••

‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§É

‡§Ö‡§• ‡§¶‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§£‡§§ ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§É ‡•§ ‡§§‡§§‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§≠‡•É‡§§‡§ø ‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§Ç ‡§π‡§ø‡§Ç‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§ú‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§¶‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§£‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§£‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§É ‡§ï‡§•‡§Æ‡§∏‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§® ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§è‡§§‡§Æ‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§∞‡•á ? ‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§§‡•á ‡§§‡•Å‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§™‡§∂‡•Å‡§π‡§ø‡§∞‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø ‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡§Ø‡§§‡•Ä‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§ß‡§®‡§Ç ‡§§‡•Å‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§π‡•á ‡§¶‡•Ä‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§§‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§µ ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ‡§®‡•à ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø‡§É ‡§§‡§§‡§É ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§ß‡§®‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§Ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§ß‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§®‡§æ‡§§‡§ø ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø‡§§‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡•ç ‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§µ‡§∏‡•Å‡§®‡•á ‡§ß‡§®‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç ‡§∏ ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§Ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§É ‡•§ ‡§Ü‡§™‡•ã ‡§π‡•à‡§µ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§¶‡§ø‡§∂‡§ø ‡§π‡•á‡§§‡§ø‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•á‡§§‡§ø‡§É ‡§ï‡§•‡§Æ‡§æ‡§™‡•ã ‡§π‡•à‡§µ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§Ö‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ ‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§¶‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§®‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡•ã ‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§§‡§ø ‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§∑‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•å‡§É ‡•§ ‡§Ö‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•à‡§µ‡•ã‡§™‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡§ø‡§§‡§É ‡§∂‡•Ä‡§§‡§ï‡§æ‡§≤‡•á ‡§® ‡§§‡§•‡§æ ‡§Ω‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§∂‡•Ä‡§§‡•ã‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§æ‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§ø‡§®‡•ã ‡§π‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡•§ ‡§™‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É ‡§Ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§ó‡•ç‡§µ‡§∏‡•Å‡§É ‡§§‡•å ‡§π‡§ø ‡§™‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§ó‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§™‡•É‡§•‡§ø‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§∏‡•Å ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É ‡§™‡§∂‡•Å‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§¶‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡§ï‡§•‡§Ç ‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§ø‡§∞‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§§‡§¶‡§æ‡§π- ‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§π‡•á‡§§‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§ø‡§∞‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§Ç (‡§§‡§§‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§æ‡§µ‡§ß‡§ø‡§∏‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•ã) ‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§ó‡•ç‡§µ‡§∏‡•Å‡§É ‡§™‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§™‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§É ‡•§ ‡§Ö‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§´‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡§®‡•ç ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§§‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§™‡§ø‡§™‡§∂‡•Å ‡§§‡§¶‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§É ‡•• ‡•ß‡•≠-‡•®‡•¶ ‡••

Eggeling
  1. Then on the right (south) side (he places one), with (VƒÅj. S. XV, 16), ‘This one on the right, the all-worker,’ the all-worker is this VƒÅyu (the wind) who blows here, for he makes everything here; and because he speaks of him as (being) ‘on the right,’ therefore it is in the south that he blows most;–‘and Rathasvana (chariot-noise) and Rathecitra (glorious on the chariot), his commander and chieftain;’ these are the two summer-months;–‘and the two nymphs, MenakƒÅ and SahajanyƒÅ,’–‘quarter and intermediate quarter,’ said MƒÅhitthi; but these two are heaven and earth;–‘Goblins the shaft, demons the missile;’ for goblins indeed are here the shaft (weapon), and demons the missile;–’to them be homage . . .!’ the import of this has been explained.

‡§Ö‡§Ø·≥ò‡§Æ‡•ç ‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§æ·≥ò‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ·≥ò‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ö‡§æ ‡§á·≥ò‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•å ‡§µ‡§æ·≥ò ‡§Ü‡§¶‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ·≥ò‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ö‡§æ ‡§Ø‡§¶‡§æ‡•ó ‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡•ó‡§µ‡•à‡§∑·≥ò ‡§â‡§¶‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø·≥ò‡§•‡•á‡§¶·≥´‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç·≥ò ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø·≥ò‡§ö‡•ã ‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§ø ‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§æ·≥ò‡§π ‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø·≥ò‡§§‡§ø ‡§§·≥ò‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡•á‡§§·≥ò‡§Æ‡•ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø·≥ò‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ ‡§Ø·≥ò‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç ‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§§·≥ò‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∞·≥ò‡§•‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§§‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§æ·≥ò‡§∏‡§Æ‡§∞‡§•‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§∏‡•á‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡•Ä‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ó‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§µ‡§ø·≥ò‡§§‡§ø ‡§µ‡§æ·≥ò‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§ï‡•å ‡§§‡§æ·≥ò‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•Ç·≥ò ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç‡§≤‡•ã·≥ò‡§ö‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•Ä ‡§ö‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§Æ‡•ç‡§≤‡•ã·≥ò‡§ö‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•Ä ‡§ö‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§∏‡§∞·≥ò‡§∏‡§æ‡§µ‡§ø·≥ò‡§§‡§ø ‡§¶‡§ø·≥ò‡§ï‡•ç‡§ö‡•ã‡§™‡§¶‡§ø‡§∂‡§æ ‡§ö‡•á·≥ò‡§§‡§ø ‡§π ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§π ‡§Æ‡§æ·≥ò‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§∞‡§π‡•ã‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•á ‡§§‡•Å ‡§§‡•á ‡§§‡•á ‡§π‡§ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞·≥ò ‡§ö ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§≤‡•ã·≥ò‡§ö‡§§‡•ã·≥ò ‡§Ω‡§®‡•Å ‡§ö ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§≤‡•ã‡§ö‡§§‡•ã ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ò‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ·≥ò ‡§π‡•á‡§§‡§ø‡§É·≥ò ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§™‡§æ‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞·≥ò‡§π‡•á‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡§ø·≥ò‡§§‡§ø ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ò‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ·≥ò ‡§π‡•à‡§µ‡§æ·≥ò‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§π‡•á‡§§‡§ø‡§É·≥ò ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§™‡§æ‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞·≥ò‡§π‡•á‡§§‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•á·≥ò‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§®·≥ò‡§Æ‡•ã ‡§Ö‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø·≥ò‡§§‡§ø‡§§·≥ò‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ã ‡§¨·≥ò‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡•Å‡§É‡••

‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§≤‡§Æ‡•ç - ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç

(‡•©) ‡§Ö‡§• ‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§æ‡§§‡•ç ‡•§ “‡§Ö‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ö‡§æ‡§É”- ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§Ö‡§∏‡•å ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§Ω‡§Ü‡§¶‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ö‡§æ‡§É ‡•§ ‡§Ø‡§¶‡§æ ‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§µ‡•à‡§∑ ‡§â‡§¶‡•á‡§§‡§ø- ‡§Ö‡§•‡•á‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ö‡•ã ‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§§‡§¶‡•ç ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§æ‡§π-‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡•á‡§§‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ ‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ “‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∞‡§•‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§§‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§æ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§∞‡§•‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§∏‡•á‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡•Ä‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡•å”- ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§ï‡•å ‡§§‡§æ‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•Ç ‡•§ “‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç‡§≤‡•ã‡§ö‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•Ä ‡§ö‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§Æ‡•ç‡§≤‡•ã‡§ö‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•Ä ‡§ö‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§∏‡§∞‡§∏‡•å”- ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§¶‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§ö‡•ã‡§™‡§¶‡§ø‡§∂‡§æ ‡§ö‡•á‡§§‡§ø ‡§π ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§π ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§É ‡•§ ‡§Ö‡§π‡•ã‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•á ‡§§‡•Å ‡§§‡•á ‡•§ ‡§§‡•á ‡§π‡§ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§ö ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§≤‡•ã‡§ö‡§§‡•ã ‡§Ω‡§®‡•Å ‡§ö ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§≤‡•ã‡§ö‡§§‡§É ‡•§ “‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ò‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ ‡§π‡•á‡§§‡§ø‡§É ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§™‡§æ‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•á‡§§‡§ø‡§É”- ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ò‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ ‡§π‡•à‡§µ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§π‡•á‡§§‡§ø‡§É, ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§™‡§æ‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•á‡§§‡§ø‡§É ‡•§ “‡§§‡•á‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§®‡§Æ‡•ã ‡§Ö‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å”- (‡§µ‡§æ. ‡§∏‡§Ç. ‡•ß‡•´ ‡•§ ‡•ß‡•≠) ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ã ‡§¨‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡•Å‡§É ‡•• ‡•ß‡•Æ ‡••

‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§É

[‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§¶‡§∂‡•á]

Eggeling
  1. Then behind (in the west, he lays down a brick), with (VƒÅj. S. XV, 17), ‘This one behind, the all-embracer,’–the all-embracer, doubtless, is yonder sun; for as soon as he rises all this embracing space comes into existence; and because he speaks of him as (being) ‘behind,’ therefore one sees him only when he goes towards the back (west);–‘and Rathaprota (fixed on the chariot) and Asamaratha (of matchless chariot), his commander and chieftain;’ these are the two rainy months;–‘and the nymphs Pramlocantƒ´ (the setting one) and

Anumlocantƒ´ (the rising one),’–‘quarter and intermediate quarter,’ said MƒÅhitthi, but they are day and night, for these two set and rise; ’tigers the shaft, snakes the missile,’ for indeed tigers are here the shaft, and snakes the missile;–’to them be homage . . .!’ the import of this has been explained.

(‡•™) ‡§Ö‡§•‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§§‡§É ‡•§ “‡§Ö‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§Ç‡§Ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§∏‡•Å‡§É”- ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡•ã ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§â‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡•ç ‡•§ ‡§§‡§¶‡•ç ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§æ‡§π‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§â‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§§‡§â‡§™‡§ö‡§æ‡§∞‡•ã ‡§π‡§ø ‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§É ‡•§ ‡§Ö‡§• ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§Ç‡§Ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§π ‡•§ ‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§Ç ‡§π‡§ø ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø- ‡§á‡§§‡•Ä‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ “‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§§‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§æ‡§∞‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§®‡•á‡§Æ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§∏‡•á‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡•Ä‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡•å”- ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§∂‡§æ‡§∞‡§¶‡•å ‡§§‡§æ‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•Ç ‡•§ “‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö‡•Ä ‡§ö ‡§ò‡•É‡§§‡§æ‡§ö‡•Ä ‡§ö‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§∏‡§∞‡§∏‡•å”- ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§¶‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§ö‡•ã‡§™‡§¶‡§ø‡§∂‡§æ ‡§ö‡•á‡§§‡§ø ‡§π ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§π- ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§É ‡•§ ‡§µ‡•á‡§¶‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§§‡•Å ‡§§‡•á ‡§∏‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§ö ‡•§ ‡§µ‡•á‡§¶‡§ø‡§∞‡•á‡§µ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö‡•Ä, ‡§∏‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§ó‡•ç‡§ò‡•É‡§§‡§æ‡§ö‡•Ä ‡•§ “‡§Ü‡§™‡•ã ‡§π‡•á‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§§‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•á‡§§‡§ø‡§É”- ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§Ü‡§™‡•ã ‡§π‡•à‡§µ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§π‡•á‡§§‡§ø‡§É, ‡§µ‡§æ‡§§‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•á‡§§‡§ø‡§É ‡•§ ‡§Ö‡§§‡•ã ‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§µ‡•ã‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡•ã ‡§µ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§É ‡§∂‡•Ä‡§§‡§É ‡•§ “‡§§‡•á‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§®‡§Æ‡•ã ‡§Ö‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å”- (‡§µ‡§æ. ‡§∏‡§Ç. ‡•ß‡•´ ‡•§ ‡•ß‡•Æ) ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ã ‡§¨‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡•Å‡§É ‡•• ‡•ß‡•Ø ‡••

‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§É

[‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§¶‡§∂‡•á]

Eggeling
  1. Then on the left (north) side (he places one), with (VƒÅj. S. XV, 17), ‘This one on the left, of ever flowing blessings;’ on the left is the sacrifice; and as to why he speaks of it as ‘on the left,’ it is because the sacrifice is performed from the left (north) side; and as to why he speaks of it as ‘of ever-flowing blessings (sa·πÅyadvasu),’ they do indeed flow together (sa·πÅyanti) to the sacrifice, thinking, ’this is a blessing;’–‘and TƒÅrkshya and Arish·π≠anemi, his commander and chieftain,’ these are the two autumn-months; ‘and the nymphs Vi≈õvƒÅcƒ´ (the all-inclined) and GhrÃ•tƒÅcƒ´ (the ghee-inclined),’–‘quarter and intermediate quarter,’ said MƒÅhitthi, but they are the vedi (altar) and the offering-spoon, for the altar is all-inclined 25, and the offering-spoon is ghee-inclined;–‘water the shaft, wind the missile,’–water indeed is here the shaft, and wind the missile, for from this side it blows hot, and from that side cold;–’to them be homage . . .!’ the import of this has been explained.

‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§≤‡§Æ‡•ç - ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç

(‡•´) ‡§Ö‡§• ‡§Æ‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á ‡•§ “‡§Ö‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•Å‡§™‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§ó‡•ç‡§µ‡§∏‡•Å‡§É”- ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§™‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§Ω‡§â‡§™‡§∞‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§æ‡§π ‡§â‡§™‡§∞‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§â‡§™‡§∞‡§ø ‡§π‡§ø ‡§™‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É ‡•§ ‡§Ö‡§• ‡§Ø‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§ó‡•ç‡§µ‡§∏‡•Å‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§π- ‡§Ö‡§§‡•ã ‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§ó‡•ç‡§µ‡§∏‡•Å-‡§µ‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§ø‡§∞‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§¶‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡•§ “‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∏‡•á‡§®‡§ú‡§ø‡§ö‡•ç‡§ö ‡§∏‡•Å‡§∑‡•á‡§£‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§∏‡•á‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡•Ä‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡•å”- ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§π‡•à‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§ï‡•å ‡§§‡§æ‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•Ç ‡•• “‡§â‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§∂‡•Ä ‡§ö ‡§™‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§∏‡§∞‡§∏‡•å”- ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§¶‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§ö‡•ã‡§™‡§¶‡§ø‡§∂‡§æ ‡§ö‡•á‡§§‡§ø ‡§π ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§π ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§É ‡•§ ‡§Ü‡§π‡•Å‡§§‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§§‡•Å ‡§§‡•á ‡§¶‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§£‡§æ ‡§ö ‡•§ “‡§Ö‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§´‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡§®‡•ç‡§π‡•á‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•á‡§§‡§ø‡§É”- ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§Ö‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§´‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡§®‡•ç‡§π‡•à‡§µ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§π‡•á‡§§‡§ø‡§É, ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•á‡§§‡§ø‡§É ‡•§ “‡§§‡•á‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§®‡§Æ‡•ã ‡§Ö‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å”- (‡§µ‡§æ‡•¶ ‡§∏‡§Ç‡•¶ ‡•ß‡•´ ‡•§ ‡•ß‡•Ø) ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ã ‡§¨‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡•Å‡§É ‡•• ‡•®‡•¶ ‡••

‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§É

[‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§¶‡§∂‡•á]

Eggeling
  1. Then in the middle (he lays down one), with (VƒÅj. S. XV, 19), ‘This one above, the boon-bestower 26,’ the one above, doubtless, is Parjanya (the rain-god); and when he speaks of him as (being)

‘above,’ it is because Parjanya is indeed above; and when he calls him the boon-bestower, it is because from there the boon, rain, food for creatures, is bestowed hitherwards;–‘and Senajit (the conqueror of armies) and Sushena (leader of a fine army), his commander and chieftain,’ these are the two winter-months;–‘and the nymphs, Urva≈õƒ´ and P≈´rva≈õcitti,’–‘quarter and intermediate quarter,’ said MƒÅhitthi, but they are oblation and dakshi·πáƒÅ (priest’s sacrificial fee);–’thunder the shaft, lightning the missile,’ for indeed thunder is here the shaft, and lightning the missile;–’to them be homage . . .!’ the import of this has been explained.

‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§É

‡§è‡§§‡•á ‡§µ‡•à ‡§§‡•á ‡§π‡•á‡§§‡§Ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•á‡§§‡§Ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§Ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§≠‡•É‡§§‡§Ø‡§É ‡•§ ‡§Ö‡§• ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§É ‡§™‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§ö‡•Ç‡§°‡§æ ‡§á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§ï‡•á ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§π‡§∞‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡§É ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•å ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§ø‡§®‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§∂‡§§‡§™‡§•‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡§≠‡§æ‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á ‡§Ω‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§Æ‡•á ‡§ï‡§æ‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡•á ‡§∑‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡•á ‡§Ω‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡•á ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§•‡§Æ‡§Ç ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡§Æ‡•ç ‡•• (‡•Æ-‡•¨-‡•ß) ‡••

Eggeling
  1. These, then, are the shafts and missiles which the gods then put as protectors over these worlds, and as to offspring (or subjects 28), they are the commander and chieftain; and as to the mates, they are those nymphs,–having thus become complete with offspring and with mates, the gods seated themselves on that firmament, in the world of heaven; and in like manner does the Sacrificer, having become complete with offspring and a mate, now seat himself on that firmament, in the world of heaven.

‡§¶‡§∂‡•á·≥ò‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§ï‡§æ ‡§â·≥ò‡§™‡§¶‡§ß‡§æ‡§§‡§ø ‡§¶·≥ò‡§∂‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§∞‡§æ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∞‡§æ·≥ò‡§°‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§∞‡§æ·≥ò‡§°‡•á‡§∑‡§æ ‡§ö‡§ø·≥ò‡§§‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§æ·≥ò ‡§â ‡§µ‡•à ‡§™·≥ò‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡•à‡§µ ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡•á·≥ò-‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡•ó ‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§™‡§¶·≥ò‡§ß‡§æ‡§§‡§ø ‡§§‡§æ·≥ò ‡§π‡•à‡§§‡§æ·≥ò ‡§Ö‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡•á·≥ò‡§∞‡§æ‡§∂‡§ø‡§∑‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§æ·≥ò ‡§â‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ö‡§ø·≥ò‡§§‡§æ ‡§â·≥ò‡§™‡§¶‡§ß‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§ ‡§è‡•ó‡§∑‡•ã ‡§Ω‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡•á‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø·≥ò‡§¶‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§ö‡§ø·≥ò‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§§·≥ò‡§¶‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡•á·≥ò‡§∞‡§æ‡§∂‡§ø·≥ò‡§∑‡•ã ‡§®‡§ø·≥ò‡§∞‡§æ‡§π ‡§™·≥ò‡§û‡•ç‡§ö ‡§≠‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§™·≥ò‡§û‡•ç‡§ö ‡§π‡§ø·≥ò ‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û·≥ò ‡§Ü‡§∂‡§ø‡§∑‡•ã·≥ò ‡§Ω‡§•‡•à‡§®‡•á ‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§æ ‡§™‡•Å·≥ò‡§∞‡•Ä‡§∑‡§Ç ‡§®‡§ø·≥ò‡§µ‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡•Ä·≥ò ‡§π‡•à‡§§‡•å ‡§Ø·≥ò‡§¶‡•á‡§§‡•á ‡§á·≥ò‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§ï‡•á ‡§®‡•á·≥ò‡§¶‡§ø‡§Æ‡§æ·≥ò‡§µ‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡•Ä·≥ò ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§∂‡•ã·≥ò‡§ö‡§æ‡§§ ‡§á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø·≥ò‡§•‡•ã ‡§Ö·≥ò‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•à ‡§™‡•Å·≥ò‡§∞‡•Ä‡§∑‡§Æ·≥ò‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡•á‡§®‡•à‡•ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡•á‡§§·≥ò‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§Ç‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§Ç·≥ò ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã‡§§‡§ø‡••

‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§≤‡§Æ‡•ç - ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç

‡§§‡§æ ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§è‡§§‡§æ ‡§¶‡§∂‡•á‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§ï‡§æ ‡§â‡§™‡§¶‡§ß‡§æ‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§¶‡§∂‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§∞‡§æ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∞‡§æ‡§ü‡•ç ‡•§ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∞‡§æ‡§°‡•á‡§∑‡§æ ‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡§ø‡§É ‡•§ ‡§§‡§æ ‡§â ‡§µ‡•à ‡§™‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡•à‡§µ ‡•§ ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡•á ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡•á ‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§™‡§¶‡§ß‡§æ‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§§‡§æ ‡§π‡•à‡§§‡§æ ‡§Ö‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡•á‡§∞‡§æ‡§∂‡§ø‡§∑‡§É ‡•§ ‡§§‡§æ ‡§â‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡§æ ‡§â‡§™‡§¶‡§ß‡§æ‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§§ ‡§è‡§∑‡•ã ‡§Ω‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡•á‡§É- ‡§Ø‡§¶‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡§ø‡§É ‡•§ ‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§¶‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡•á‡§∞‡§æ‡§∂‡§ø‡§∑‡•ã ‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡§æ‡§π ‡•§ ‡§™‡§û‡•ç‡§ö ‡§≠‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§™‡§û‡•ç‡§ö ‡§π‡§ø ‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û ‡§Ü‡§∂‡§ø‡§∑‡§É ‡•§ ‡§Ö‡§•‡•à‡§®‡•á ‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§æ ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Ä‡§∑‡§Ç ‡§®‡§ø‡§µ‡§™‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§Ö‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡•Ä ‡§π‡•à‡§§‡•å- ‡§Ø‡§¶‡•á‡§§‡•á ‡§á‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§ï‡•á ‡•§ ‡§®‡•á‡§¶‡§ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§µ‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡•Ä ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§∂‡•ã‡§ö‡§æ‡§§ ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§Ö‡§•‡•ã ‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•à ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Ä‡§∑‡§Æ‡•ç ‡•§ ‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡•á‡§®‡•à‡§µ‡§æ‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡•á‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§Ç‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã‡§§‡§ø ‡•• ‡•®‡•® ‡••

‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§É

[‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§è‡§ï‡§µ‡§ø‡§Ç‡§∂‡§§‡§ø‡§§‡§Æ‡•á]

Eggeling
  1. Now, these are ten (NƒÅkasad-Pa√±cac≈´·∏çƒÅ) bricks he lays down;–of ten, syllables the VirƒÅj consists, and this layer is virƒÅj (far-shining). There are, however, only five of them, for he lays them down by two and two. And, verily, they are prayers for prosperity to Agni (the fire-altar). He places them in the last layer, for this, the last, layer is the end of Agni: it is thus at the end that he

pronounces the prayers for prosperity to Agni. There are five of them, for at the sacrifice there are five prayers for prosperity 29. Between (each) two he throws loose soil, for these two bricks being fires, he does so fearing lest these two fires should blaze up together. And, moreover, loose soil means food: it is thus by means of food that he brings about concord between them.

‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§É

[‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§è‡§ï‡§µ‡§ø‡§Ç‡§∂‡§§‡§ø‡§§‡§Æ‡•á]

Eggeling
  1. Now; then, as to the order of proceeding. Having laid down (a brick) in front, he lays down those on the right, behind, on the left, and in the middle. Then the upper ones: having first laid down one in front, he lays down those on the right, on the left, in the middle, and behind. And, indeed, the world of heaven is entered from below, for the gods, having at that time, closed up these worlds on all sides, entered the world of heaven from below; and in like manner does the Sacrificer now, having closed up these worlds on all sides, enter the world of heaven from below.

  1. ‡§®‡§æ‡§ï‡§∏‡§¶‡•ã ‡§Ω‡§®‡•Ç‡§ï‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§™‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•ç‡§µ‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡§Æ‡•É‡§§‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§µ‡•á‡§≤‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§®‡•Ä‡§µ‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§Æ‡§Ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç ‡•§ ‡§ï‡§æ. ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•å. ‡§∏‡•Ç. ‡•ß‡•≠ ‡•§ ‡•®‡•©‡•¨ ‡•§ ↩︎

  2. 97:1 The central portion of the fifth layer is here characterised as symbolically representing the firmament, the blue canopy of heaven, and the region of bliss beyond it. The outer rim of this central structure is formed by a continuous ring of twenty-nine StomabhƒÅgƒÅ (st) bricks representing, it would seem, the horizon on which the vault of heaven rests. There is some doubt as to the exact manner in which this ring of bricks is to be arranged. According to KƒÅty. ≈örautas. XVII, 11, 10, fifteen bricks are to he placed south (and fourteen north) of the an≈´ka, or spine (running through the centre from west to east). As regards the southern semicircle, the fifteen bricks are to be distributed in such a way that eight fall within the south-easterly, and seven into the south-westerly, quadrant. Some such arrangement as that adopted in the diagram below would seem to be what is intended. It will be seen that this arrangement includes two half-size bricks in the south-easterly ↩︎

  3. i.e. ‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§É‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ã‡§Æ‡§≠‡§æ‡§ó‡§Æ‡•ç ↩︎

  4. ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§π‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•á·≥ò‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø A. ↩︎

  5. 100:1 Or, perhaps, ’the Vasus are thy divine overlords;’ but see paragraph 9. ↩︎

  6. 100:2 Lit. for unwaveringness (so as not to totter). ↩︎

  7. 100:3 Lit. broaden, widen. ↩︎
